However, in the final metres of the [2002 Austrian Grand Prix](/wiki/2002_Austrian_Grand_Prix "2002 Austrian Grand Prix") , Schumacher's teammate, [Rubens Barrichello](/wiki/Rubens_Barrichello "Rubens Barrichello") , slowed his car under orders from Ferrari to allow Schumacher to pass and win the race. [\[71\]](#cite_note-bbcaustria-71 "") Although the switching of positions did not break any actual sporting or technical regulation, it angered fans and it was claimed that the team's actions showed a lack of sportsmanship and respect to the spectators. Many argued that Schumacher did not need to be "given" wins in only the 6th race of the season, particularly given that he had already won four of the previous five grands prix, and that Barrichello had dominated the race weekend up to that point. At the podium ceremony, Schumacher pushed Barrichello onto the top step, [\[71\]](#cite_note-bbcaustria-71 "") and for this disturbance, the Ferrari team incurred a US$1 million fine. [\[156\]](#cite_note-156 "") Later in the season at the end of the [2002 United States Grand Prix](/wiki/2002_United_States_Grand_Prix "2002 United States Grand Prix") , Schumacher slowed down within sight of the finishing line, allowing Barrichello to win by 0.011 seconds, the 2nd closest margin in F1 history. Schumacher's explanation varied between it being him "returning the favour" for Austria \(now that Schumacher's title was secure\), or trying to engineer a dead\-heat \(a feat derided as near\-impossible in a sport where timings are taken to within a thousandth of a second\). [\[157\]](#cite_note-157 "") The FIA subsequently banned "team orders which interfere with the race result", [\[158\]](#cite_note-158 "") [\[159\]](#cite_note-159 "") but the ban was lifted for the 2011 season because the ruling was difficult to enforce. [\[160\]](#cite_note-160 "") 

### Dangerous driving \[ [edit](/w/index.php?title=Michael_Schumacher&action=edit§ion=25 "Edit section: Dangerous driving") \]

During his spell in [Sauber](/wiki/Sauber "Sauber") , in the 1991 Sportscar World Championship, Schumacher was involved in a serious incident with [Derek Warwick](/wiki/Derek_Warwick "Derek Warwick") in that year's [430 km of Nürburgring](/wiki/1991_430_km_of_N%C3%BCrburgring "1991 430 km of Nürburgring") . While trying to set his flying lap in qualifying, Schumacher encountered Warwick's [Jaguar](/wiki/Jaguar_XJR-14 "Jaguar XJR-14") on a slow lap resulting in lost time for Schumacher. As retaliation for being in his way, Schumacher swerved the Sauber into Warwick's car, hitting the Jaguar's nose and front wheel. Enraged by the German's attitude, Warwick drove to the pits and chased a fleeing Schumacher on foot through the Sauber pits. He eventually caught up with Schumacher, and it took intervention from [Jochen Mass](/wiki/Jochen_Mass "Jochen Mass") to prevent Warwick physically assaulting Schumacher. [\[161\]](#cite_note-161 "") 

Toward the end of the [2010 Hungarian Grand Prix](/wiki/2010_Hungarian_Grand_Prix "2010 Hungarian Grand Prix") , [Rubens Barrichello](/wiki/Rubens_Barrichello "Rubens Barrichello") attempted to pass Schumacher down the inside on the main straight. Schumacher closed the inside line to force Barrichello onto the outside, but Barrichello persisted on the inside at 180 mph \(290 km/h\), despite the close proximity of a concrete wall and Schumacher leaving him only inches to spare. Barrichello said "It is the most dangerous thing that I have been through", and "There is not a rule for that, but between ourselves we should take a line, stick to it and that's it." Schumacher said that "Obviously there was space enough to go through. We didn't touch, so I guess I just left enough space for him to come through." Ross Brawn said "at the end of the day he gave him enough space. You can argue that it was marginal, but it was just tough – tough racing." A range of ex\-drivers and commentators were highly critical of Schumacher. Although there was no accident, the race steward, the same Derek Warwick of the 1991 Nürburgring incident, wanted to black flag Schumacher since that "would have shown a better example to our young drivers". The Hungaroring incident was ruled to be dangerous and Schumacher received a 10 place grid penalty for the [next race](/wiki/2010_Belgian_Grand_Prix "2010 Belgian Grand Prix") . Schumacher accepted the decision, and apologised. [\[162\]](#cite_note-162 "") [\[163\]](#cite_note-163 "") [\[164\]](#cite_note-164 "") [\[165\]](#cite_note-165 "") [\[166\]](#cite_note-166 "") [\[167\]](#cite_note-167 "") 

### Other incidents \[ [edit](/w/index.php?title=Michael_Schumacher&action=edit§ion=26 "Edit section: Other incidents") \]

In 1994, suspicion of foul play by the Benetton team \(who were eventually found to have been responsible for some [technical violations](/wiki/1994_Formula_One_cheating_controversy "1994 Formula One cheating controversy") over the course of the season\) was said to have troubled Ayrton Senna that season. For example, in the words of his then teammate, Damon Hill, Senna had chosen to spend a bit of time at the first corner of the Aida circuit following his retirement from the [Pacific Grand Prix](/wiki/1994_Pacific_Grand_Prix "1994 Pacific Grand Prix") . After listening to Schumacher's [Benetton B194](/wiki/Benetton_B194 "Benetton B194") as it went past, Senna "concluded that there was, what he regarded, as unusual noises from the engine". [\[168\]](#cite_note-168 "") The FIA subsequently issued a press release setting out action that it required teams to take prior to the [German Grand Prix](/wiki/1994_German_Grand_Prix "1994 German Grand Prix") , given that various cars were found to have an advanced engine management systems emulating launch and traction control. [\[169\]](#cite_note-169 "") [\[170\]](#cite_note-170 "") 

In 1995, Schumacher and Williams driver [David Coulthard](/wiki/David_Coulthard "David Coulthard") were disqualified for fuel irregularities, after a switch to Renault engines and Elf oils. [\[171\]](#cite_note-171 "") On appeal, both drivers had their results and points reinstated, but both teams lost the points the results would normally have earned in the Constructors' Championship. [\[172\]](#cite_note-172 "") 

The 1998 Canadian Grand Prix saw Schumacher accused of dangerous driving when his exit from the pit\-lane forced [Heinz\-Harald Frentzen](/wiki/Heinz-Harald_Frentzen "Heinz-Harald Frentzen") off the track and into retirement. Despite receiving a 10\-second penalty, Schumacher recovered and won the race. [\[173\]](#cite_note-173 "") 

Two laps from the finish of the [1998 British Grand Prix](/wiki/1998_British_Grand_Prix "1998 British Grand Prix") , Schumacher was leading the race when he was issued a stop\-and\-go penalty for overtaking a lapped car \( [Alexander Wurz](/wiki/Alexander_Wurz "Alexander Wurz") \) during the early moments of a [Safety Car](/wiki/Safety_Car "Safety Car") period. This penalty involves going into the pit lane and stopping for 10 seconds, and the rules state that a driver must serve his penalty within three laps of the penalty being issued. On the third lap after receiving the penalty, Schumacher turned into the pit lane to serve his penalty, but as this was the last lap of the race, and as Ferrari's pit box was located after the start/finish line, Schumacher technically finished the race before serving the penalty. The stewards initially resolved that problem by adding 10 seconds to Schumacher's race time, then later rescinded the penalty completely due to the irregularities in how the penalty had been issued. [\[174\]](#cite_note-174 "") 

In the [1998 Belgian Grand Prix](/wiki/1998_Belgian_Grand_Prix "1998 Belgian Grand Prix") , Schumacher was involved in a race\-ending collision whilst trying to lap [David Coulthard](/wiki/David_Coulthard "David Coulthard") in heavy spray. After the race he stormed into the [McLaren](/wiki/McLaren "McLaren") garage and accused Coulthard of trying to kill him, and McLaren and Ferrari team members had to separate the drivers. Coulthard admitted some five years later that the accident had been his mistake. [\[63\]](#cite_note-spa98-63 "") 

During qualifying for the [2006 Monaco Grand Prix](/wiki/2006_Monaco_Grand_Prix "2006 Monaco Grand Prix") Schumacher set the fastest time, but his car stopped in the Rascasse corner on the racing line, leaving the corner partially blocked, while his main contender for the season title, [Fernando Alonso](/wiki/Fernando_Alonso "Fernando Alonso") , was on his final qualifying lap. Schumacher stated that he simply locked up the wheels going into the corner and that the car then stalled while he attempted to reverse out. [\[175\]](#cite_note-monacopole-175 "") Alonso believed he would have been on pole if the incident had not happened, [\[176\]](#cite_note-176 "") and Schumacher was stripped of pole position by the race stewards and started the race at the back of the grid. [\[175\]](#cite_note-monacopole-175 "") In the same qualifying session, [Giancarlo Fisichella](/wiki/Giancarlo_Fisichella "Giancarlo Fisichella") was similarly found to have blocked [David Coulthard](/wiki/David_Coulthard "David Coulthard") from improving his time, but Fisichella was only demoted five places on the grid. [\[177\]](#cite_note-fisichella-drop-177 "") At the [2010 Monaco Grand Prix](/wiki/2010_Monaco_Grand_Prix "2010 Monaco Grand Prix") , the safety car was deployed after an accident, involving [Karun Chandhok](/wiki/Karun_Chandhok "Karun Chandhok") and [Jarno Trulli](/wiki/Jarno_Trulli "Jarno Trulli") , and pulled into the pits on the last lap. Schumacher passed Alonso before the finish line. Mercedes held that "the combination of the race control messages 'Safety Car in this lap' and 'Track Clear' and the green flags and lights shown by the marshals after safety car line one indicated that the race was not finishing under the safety car and all drivers were free to race. This opinion appears to have been shared by the majority of the teams with cars in the top ten positions who also gave their drivers instructions to race to the finish line." [\[178\]](#cite_note-178 "") However an FIA investigation found Schumacher guilty of breaching Safety Car regulations and awarded him a 20\-seconds penalty, which cost him six places.\[ *[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")* \]

## Personal life \[ [edit](/w/index.php?title=Michael_Schumacher&action=edit§ion=27 "Edit section: Personal life") \]

Michael Schumacher 
Michael Schumacher in 2007Born \( 1969\-01\-03 \) 3 January 1969 \(age 48\) 
[Hürth](/wiki/H%C3%BCrth "Hürth") , [West Germany](/wiki/West_Germany "West Germany") NationalityGermanOccupation

- Racing driver
- philanthropist

Spouse\(s\) [Corinna Betsch](/wiki/Corinna_Schumacher "Corinna Schumacher") \(m. 1995\) Children

- Gina\-Maria Schumacher \(daughter\)
- [Mick Schumacher](/wiki/Mick_Schumacher "Mick Schumacher") \(son\)

Relatives

- [Ralf Schumacher](/wiki/Ralf_Schumacher "Ralf Schumacher") \(brother\)
- [Sebastian Stahl](/wiki/Sebastian_Stahl "Sebastian Stahl") \(stepbrother\)

Website [michael\-schumacher.de](http://www.michael-schumacher.de/ "") Signature

Schumacher's younger brother [Ralf](/wiki/Ralf_Schumacher "Ralf Schumacher") was a Formula One driver until the end of 2007. [\[13\]](#cite_note-schumacher_hof-13 "") Their stepbrother [Sebastian Stahl](/wiki/Sebastian_Stahl "Sebastian Stahl") has also been a racing driver. [\[179\]](#cite_note-179 "") 

In August 1995, Michael married [Corinna Betsch](/wiki/Corinna_Schumacher "Corinna Schumacher") . [\[180\]](#cite_note-180 "") They have two children, a daughter Gina\-Marie, born in 1997 and a son [Mick](/wiki/Mick_Schumacher "Mick Schumacher") , born March 22, 1999. He has always been very protective of his private life [\[181\]](#cite_note-181 "") and is known to dislike the celebrity spotlight. The family moved to a newly\-built mansion near [Gland, Switzerland](/wiki/Gland,_Switzerland "Gland, Switzerland") in 2007, covering an area of 650\-square\-metre \(7,000 sq ft\) with a private beach on [Lake Geneva](/wiki/Lake_Geneva "Lake Geneva") and featuring an underground garage and petrol station. [\[182\]](#cite_note-182 "") 

Schumacher and his wife own horse ranches in [Texas](/wiki/Texas "Texas") [\[183\]](#cite_note-183 "") and Switzerland. [\[184\]](#cite_note-184 "") 

The family has two dogs – one stray that Corinna fell in love with in Brazil, and an [Australian Shepherd](/wiki/Australian_Shepherd "Australian Shepherd") named "Ed" whose arrival in the family made headlines. In fact, in 2007, Schumacher personally drove a taxi through the Bavarian town of [Coburg](/wiki/Coburg "Coburg") to collect the dog and enable the family to make their return flight to Switzerland. [\[185\]](#cite_note-185 "") Both Schumacher and the taxi driver were reprimanded by local police. [\[186\]](#cite_note-186 "") 

One of his main hobbies is horse riding, and he plays [football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") for his local team [FC Echichens](/wiki/FC_Echichens "FC Echichens") . He has appeared in several charity football games [\[187\]](#cite_note-fifa-charity_football-187 "") and organised games between Formula One drivers. [\[188\]](#cite_note-schumacher_retirement_response_thoughts-188 "") 

On 23 June 2003, Schumacher was appointed as an [Ambassador\-at\-Large](/wiki/Ambassador-at-Large "Ambassador-at-Large") for the [Most Serene Republic of San Marino](/wiki/Most_Serene_Republic_of_San_Marino "Most Serene Republic of San Marino") . [\[189\]](#cite_note-189 "") [\[190\]](#cite_note-190 "") 

Schumacher is a special ambassador to [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") and has donated 1.5 million euros to the organization. [\[191\]](#cite_note-unesco-champion_for_sport-191 "") Additionally, he paid for the construction of a school for poor children and for area improvements in [Dakar](/wiki/Dakar "Dakar") , Senegal. He supports a hospital for child victims of war in [Sarajevo](/wiki/Sarajevo "Sarajevo") , which specialises in caring for amputees. In [Lima](/wiki/Lima "Lima") , Peru he funded the "Palace for the Poor", a centre for helping homeless street children obtain an education, clothing, food, medical attention, and shelter. He stated his interest in these various efforts was piqued both by his love for children and the fact that these causes had received little attention. While an exact figure for the amount of money he has donated throughout his life is unknown, it is known that in his last four years as a driver, he donated at least $50 million. [\[10\]](#cite_note-donated50mil-10 "") In 2008, it was revealed that he had donated between $5M and $10M to the [William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park](/wiki/William_J._Clinton_Presidential_Center_and_Park "William J. Clinton Presidential Center and Park") of [Bill Clinton](/wiki/Bill_Clinton "Bill Clinton") . [\[192\]](#cite_note-Clinton_Foundation_Donors-192 "") 

Since his participation in an FIA European road safety campaign, as part of his punishment after the collision at the [1997 European Grand Prix](/wiki/1997_European_Grand_Prix "1997 European Grand Prix") , Schumacher continued to support other campaigns, such as [Make Roads Safe](/wiki/Make_Roads_Safe "Make Roads Safe") , which is led by the FIA Foundation and calls on [G8](/wiki/G8 "G8") countries and the UN to recognise global road deaths as a major global health issue. In 2008, Schumacher was the figurehead of an advertising campaign by [Bacardi](/wiki/Bacardi "Bacardi") to raise awareness about responsible drinking, with a focus on communicating an international message 'drinking and driving don't mix'. He featured in an advertising campaign for television, cinema and online media, supported by consumer engagements, public relations and digital media across the World. [\[193\]](#cite_note-drinkdrive-193 "") 

On the eve of the [2002 British Grand Prix](/wiki/2002_British_Grand_Prix "2002 British Grand Prix") , on behalf of Fiat, Schumacher presented a [Ferrari 360 Modena](/wiki/Ferrari_360_Modena "Ferrari 360 Modena") to the [Indian cricketer](/wiki/Cricket_in_India "Cricket in India") [Sachin Tendulkar](/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar "Sachin Tendulkar") at [Silverstone](/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit "Silverstone Circuit") . [\[194\]](#cite_note-194 "") 

On 21 June 2009, Schumacher appeared on the [BBC](/wiki/BBC "BBC") 's motoring programme *[Top Gear](/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series) "Top Gear (2002 TV series)")* as [the Stig](/wiki/The_Stig "The Stig") . [\[195\]](#cite_note-Stig-195 "") Presenter [Jeremy Clarkson](/wiki/Jeremy_Clarkson "Jeremy Clarkson") hinted later in the programme that Schumacher was not the regular Stig, and the BBC has since confirmed that this is the case. Schumacher was there on that occasion because Ferrari would not allow anyone else to drive the one\-of\-a\-kind black [Ferrari FXX](/wiki/Ferrari_FXX "Ferrari FXX") that was featured in the show. [\[196\]](#cite_note-196 "") The FXX was presented to Schumacher upon his retirement at Monza in 2006.\[ *[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")* \]

During his interview with Clarkson, Schumacher stated that his road cars are a [Fiat 500 Abarth](/wiki/Fiat_500_(2007)#Abarth_500_.282008-.29 "Fiat 500 (2007)") , and a [Fiat Croma](/wiki/Fiat_Croma "Fiat Croma") , which is his family car. [\[197\]](#cite_note-197 "") 

### Finance and sponsorship \[ [edit](/w/index.php?title=Michael_Schumacher&action=edit§ion=28 "Edit section: Finance and sponsorship") \]

In 2004, *Forbes* magazine listed him as the second highest paid athlete in the World. [\[198\]](#cite_note-198 "") In 2005, *Eurobusiness* magazine identified Schumacher as the World's first billionaire athlete. His 2004 salary was reported to be around US$80 million. [\[199\]](#cite_note-schumacher_pay-199 "") [Forbes magazine](/wiki/Forbes "Forbes") ranked him 17th in its "The World's Most Powerful Celebrities" list. [\[200\]](#cite_note-forbes_celeb_100_2005-200 "") A significant share of his income came from advertising. For example, [Deutsche Vermögensberatung](/wiki/Deutsche_Verm%C3%B6gensberatung "Deutsche Vermögensberatung") paid him $8 million over three years from 1999 for wearing a 10 by 8 centimetre advertisement on his post\-race cap. [\[201\]](#cite_note-201 "") The deal was extended until 2010. [\[202\]](#cite_note-202 "") He donated $10 million for aid after the [2004 Indian Ocean earthquake](/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake "2004 Indian Ocean earthquake") . [\[203\]](#cite_note-cnn-tsunami_relief-203 "") His donation surpassed that of any other sports person, most sports leagues, many worldwide corporations and even some countries. [\[204\]](#cite_note-si-sportsman_of_the_year-204 "") Schumacher's bodyguard Burkhard Cramer and Cramer's two sons were killed in the tsunami. [\[205\]](#cite_note-205 "") 

In 2010, his personal fortune was estimated at £515 million. [\[206\]](#cite_note-206 "") He reportedly received a salary of £21 million each year from the Mercedes team, plus a further £9 million in endorsements. [\[207\]](#cite_note-30m_comeback-207 "") 

### 2013 skiing accident \[ [edit](/w/index.php?title=Michael_Schumacher&action=edit§ion=29 "Edit section: 2013 skiing accident") \]

On 29 December 2013, Schumacher was skiing with his 14\-year\-old son [Mick](/wiki/Mick_Schumacher "Mick Schumacher") , descending the Combe de Saulire below the [Dent de Burgin](/wiki/Dent_de_Burgin "Dent de Burgin") above [Méribel](/wiki/M%C3%A9ribel "Méribel") in the [French Alps](/wiki/French_Alps "French Alps") . While crossing an unsecured [off\-piste](/wiki/Off-piste "Off-piste") area between Piste Chamois and Piste Mauduit, [\[208\]](#cite_note-208 "") [\[209\]](#cite_note-209 "") he fell and hit his head on a rock, sustaining a serious head injury despite wearing a [ski helmet](/wiki/Ski_helmet "Ski helmet") . According to his physicians, he would most likely have died if he had not been wearing a helmet. [\[210\]](#cite_note-210 "") Schumacher was put into a medically [induced coma](/wiki/Induced_coma "Induced coma") because of [traumatic brain injury](/wiki/Traumatic_brain_injury "Traumatic brain injury") ; his doctors reported on 7 March 2014 that his condition was stable. [\[211\]](#cite_note-CNN2014-03-07-211 "") [\[212\]](#cite_note-Autosport-postop-212 "") On 4 April 2014, Schumacher's agent reported that he was showing "moments of consciousness" as he was gradually withdrawn from the medically induced coma, adding to reports by relatives of "small encouraging signs" over the preceding month. [\[213\]](#cite_note-213 "") In mid\-June he was moved from intensive care into a rehabilitation ward. [\[214\]](#cite_note-Mirror20140613-214 "") By 16 June 2014, Schumacher had regained consciousness and left Grenoble Hospital for further rehabilitation at the [University Hospital \(CHUV\)](/wiki/University_Hospital_of_Lausanne "University Hospital of Lausanne") in [Lausanne](/wiki/Lausanne "Lausanne") , Switzerland. [\[215\]](#cite_note-215 "") On 9 September 2014, Schumacher left CHUV and was brought back to his home for further rehabilitation. [\[12\]](#cite_note-goinghome-12 "") In November 2014, it was reported that Schumacher was "paralysed and in a wheelchair"; he "cannot speak and has memory problems". [\[216\]](#cite_note-Schumacher_in_Nov_2014-216 "") In a video interview released in May 2015, Schumacher's manager Sabine Kehm said that his condition is slowly improving "considering the severeness of the injury he had". [\[217\]](#cite_note-217 "") 

In September 2016, Felix Damm, Schumacher's lawyer, told a German court that his client "cannot walk", in response to false reports from December 2015 in German publication *Die Bunte* that he could "walk a couple of steps". [\[218\]](#cite_note-218 "") [\[219\]](#cite_note-219 "")

‡ Schumacher was disqualified from the 1997 World Drivers' Championship due to dangerous driving in the [European Grand Prix](/wiki/1997_European_Grand_Prix "1997 European Grand Prix") , where he caused an avoidable accident with Jacques Villeneuve. His points tally would have placed him in second place in that year's standings. [\[62\]](#cite_note-fia97verdict-62 "") 
† Driver did not finish the Grand Prix, but was classified as he completed over 90% of the race distance.

- Henry, Alan \(1996\). *Wheel to Wheel: Great Duels of Formula One Racing* . Weidenfeld Nicolson Illustrated. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [0\-7538\-0522\-7](/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7538-0522-7 "Special:BookSources/0-7538-0522-7") .
- Hilton, Christopher \(2003\). *Michael Schumacher: The greatest of all* . Haynes. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [1\-84425\-044\-X](/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-84425-044-X "Special:BookSources/1-84425-044-X") .
- Hilton, Christopher \(2006\). *Michael Schumacher: The Whole Story* . Haynes. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [1\-84425\-008\-3](/wiki/Special:BookSources/1-84425-008-3 "Special:BookSources/1-84425-008-3") .
- Kehm, Sabine \(2003\). *Michael Schumacher. Driving Force* . Random House. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [0\-09\-189435\-2](/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-09-189435-2 "Special:BookSources/0-09-189435-2") .
- [Matchett, Steve](/wiki/Steve_Matchett "Steve Matchett") \(1995\). *Life in the Fast Lane: The Story of the Benetton Grand Prix Year* . London: Weidenfeld and Nicolson. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [0\-297\-81610\-1](/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-297-81610-1 "Special:BookSources/0-297-81610-1") .
- Matchett, Steve \(1999\). *The Mechanic's Tale: Life in the Pit Lanes of Formula One* . Osceola, Wisconsin: MBI Pub. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [0\-7603\-0754\-7](/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7603-0754-7 "Special:BookSources/0-7603-0754-7") .
- Williams, Richard \(1999\). *The Death of Ayrton Senna* . Bloomsbury. [ISBN](/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number "International Standard Book Number")   [0\-7475\-4495\-6](/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-7475-4495-6 "Special:BookSources/0-7475-4495-6") .

Schumacher had a voice role in the [Disney](/wiki/Disney "Disney") / [Pixar](/wiki/Pixar "Pixar") film *[Cars](/wiki/Cars_(film) "Cars (film)")* . His character is himself as a car \( [Ferrari F430](/wiki/Ferrari_F430 "Ferrari F430") \). The French film *[Asterix and Obelix at the Olympic Games](/wiki/Asterix_at_the_Olympic_Games_(film) "Asterix at the Olympic Games (film)")* features Schumacher in a cameo role, also as himself.
